         <tei:p>DIFFLUGIDAE FROM YUGOSLAVIA 369</tei:p>
         <tei:p>MEASUREMENTS (in um). One specimen: body length 97, breadth 54, diameter of aperture 29.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>REMARKS. This species is similar to D. elegans or D. bicornis (see p. 000) in having a single<tei:lb/>aboral spine or horn. However, both of these latter species are described as having a rough,<tei:lb/>irregular surface made of angular quartz particles and diatom frustules. In addition, D.<tei:lb/>elegans has a slight constriction of the neck which gives the aperture a flared appearance<tei:lb/>(Ogden, 1979), and it was found in the Yugoslavian portion of the sample to show these<tei:lb/>features (Fig. 21). Although D. styla shares similar dimensions to D. serrata (see p. 000) the<tei:lb/>presence of an aboral spine separates these species. D. styla is distinct in being elongate ovoid<tei:lb/>with an aboral spine, and having a smooth shell composed of flat particles.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Genus CUCURBITELLA Penard, 1902</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Cucurbitella vlasinensis sp. nov.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DESCRIPTION. The shell is brown or opaque, subcircular or ovoid, with a distinct apertural<tei:lb/>collar (Fig. 22a). It is composed of a mixture of small to medium pieces of quartz to give a<tei:lb/>rough surface, but arranged so that the outline is more or less regular. The particles are<tei:lb/>packed close together (Fig. 220, with only small areas of organic cement visible. The cement<tei:lb/>is in the form of a network whose mesh is covered by a smooth membrane (Fig. 22e). The<tei:lb/>collar is trilobed and composed of small pieces of quartz arranged randomly (Fig. 22b). A<tei:lb/>double thickness of particles strengthens the three tooth-like projections where they form a<tei:lb/>dividing barrier with the inner apertural opening; these 'teeth' are usually well denned and<tei:lb/>composed of small particles. Each lobe has a small recess or cavity so that the internal<tei:lb/>opening is smaller than the external collar, the floor of these recesses appears as a con-<tei:lb/>tinuation of the shell matrix (Fig. 22d). The apertural opening is trilobed in sequence with<tei:lb/>the collar and lined with flattish pieces of quartz with smaller pieces filling the junctions (Fig.<tei:lb/>22c).</tei:p>
         <tei:p>MEASUREMENTS (in um). Forty-one specimens: body length 81-1 13, breadth 69-97, diameter<tei:lb/>of collar 36-5 1 , depth of collar 9-16, diameter of aperture 1 9-35.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>REMARKS. In a review of the genus Cucurbitella by Gauthier-Lievre &amp; Thomas (1960) the<tei:lb/>number of lobes surrounding the aperture was used to differentiate species into a number of<tei:lb/>varieties and forms. More recently, Ogden (19806) considered that the three and four lobed<tei:lb/>specimens of C. mespiliformis were otherwise identical in all but that feature, and should<tei:lb/>therefore be designated as a single species until adequate morphological information was<tei:lb/>available on the variability of lobe formation. Nevertheless, observations on the many speci-<tei:lb/>mens of the present sample show that there is little or no variation in the number and shape<tei:lb/>of the lobes. C. vlasinensis is similar to C. modesta Gauthier-Lievre &amp; Thomas, 1960 and C.<tei:lb/>modesta forma trilobata Gauthier-Lievre &amp; Thomas, 1960. It differs from C. modesta, which<tei:lb/>has four lobes, in that feature and general measurements, and from C. modesta forma<tei:lb/>trilobata in having well-defined teeth, a more extensive inner lining to each lobe and in over-<tei:lb/>all larger general dimensions.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>An interesting ecological point to note is that C. modesta forma trilobata was reported<tei:lb/>only from Morocco which has similar climatic conditions to the region of Yugoslavia<tei:lb/>where the present samples were collected.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>ETYMOLOGY. This species is named after the location where the samples were collected, Lake<tei:lb/>Vlasina, and which, after a visit by both authors in 1 982, has become especially significant.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Genus PONTIGULAS1A Rhumbler, 1895</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Pontigulasia bryophila Penard, 1902</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DESCRIPTION. The shell is pyriform, tapering from the aperture to the slightly swollen<tei:lb/>posterior third of the body (Fig. 23a). It has a rough surface composed of a mixture of quartz<tei:lb/>particles with an occasional diatom frustule added. Organic cement is seen at the junctions</tei:p>
         <tei:pb/>
      </tei:div>
      <tei:div>
         <tei:p>C. G. OGDEN &amp; A. 2IVKOVIC</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Fig. 22 Cucurbitella vlasinensis sp. nov.: a, lateral view x 830; b, apertural view x 540; c, view to<tei:lb/>illustrate the arrangement of particles around the collar x 1200; d, detail of aperture to show<tei:lb/>tooth-like projections and smaller internal opening x 1200; e, detail of organic cement<tei:lb/>(arrowed) x 1 3000; f, portion of shell surface showing the close packing of particles x 1 500.</tei:p>
         <tei:pb/>
      </tei:div>
      <tei:div>
         <tei:p>DIFFLUGIDAE FROM YUGOSLAVIA</tei:p>
         <tei:p>371</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Fig. 23 Pontigulasia bryophila: a, lateral view x 470; b, view inside external aperture to show the<tei:lb/>internal aperture opening (arrowed), micrograph obtained by 'expanded contrast' facility<tei:lb/>x4100; c, apertural view x760; d, detail of organic cement to illustrate the smaller irregular<tei:lb/>network of each mesh enclosure x 29000.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>between particles as a network. This network has a mesh about 600 nm in diameter<tei:lb/>separated by walls 200 nm thick. Each enclosure has a smaller irregular network over its<tei:lb/>surface (Fig. 23d). The external aperture is small, surrounded by small or medium particles<tei:lb/>often arranged to give a serrated or tooth-like margin (Fig. 23c). The single, internal aperture<tei:lb/>is roughly circular (Fig. 23b) and positioned about a quarter of the body length from the<tei:lb/>external aperture.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>MEASUREMENTS (in urn). See Table 2.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>REMARKS. This species is similar in general appearance to Difflugia bryophila but may be<tei:lb/>distinguished from it by the presence of an internal aperture and a different organic cement<tei:lb/>pattern. The present specimens are similar in most respects to specimens of P. bryophila<tei:lb/>found in England (C.G.O. pers. observ.) except for a difference in organic cement patterns.<tei:lb/>This feature alone is not considered sufficient for specific recognition.</tei:p>
         <tei:pb/>
      </tei:div>
      <tei:div>
         <tei:p>372</tei:p>
         <tei:p>C. G. OGDEN &amp; A. ZlVKOVIC</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Pontigulasia montana sp. nov.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DESCRIPTION. The shell is pyriform, bluntly rounded aborally for one-third of its length and<tei:lb/>usually tapering gradually from the widest point towards the aperture (Fig. 24a), although<tei:lb/>sometimes there is a distinct constriction at the position of the internal aperture (Fig. 24c). It<tei:lb/>is composed of a mixture of mainly medium to large pieces of quartz arranged to give a rough<tei:lb/>surface. Organic cement is often seen as part of the shell matrix (Fig. 24d), in the form of an</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Fig. 24 Pontigulasia montana sp. nov.: a, lateral view of specimen without neck constriction<tei:lb/>x 730; b, apertural view with the internal aperture arrowed x 730; c, lateral view of specimen<tei:lb/>with distinct neck constriction x430; d, portion of shell surface showing organic cement as part<tei:lb/>of the shell matrix x4400; e, detail of organic cement network x 14000.</tei:p>
         <tei:pb/>
      </tei:div>
      <tei:div>
         <tei:p>DIFFLUGIDAE FROM YUGOSLAVIA 373</tei:p>
         <tei:p>open network with walls 200 nm thick and a mesh diameter of 400 nm (Fig. 24e). The<tei:lb/>external aperture is roughly circular and surrounded by small or medium particles randomly<tei:lb/>positioned to give it an irregular margin (Fig. 24b). The smaller, single, internal aperture is<tei:lb/>also circular and surrounded by small particles overlaid with organic cement.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>MEASUREMENTS (in um). See Table 3.<tei:lb/>Table 3 Range of measurements (in um) of two species ofPontigulasia</tei:p>
         <tei:p>REMARKS. The specimens described here are similar to Pontigulasia bryophila Penard, 1902,<tei:lb/>but the latter species has a more streamlined, elongate shell, with smaller internal and<tei:lb/>external openings, plus a distinct organic cement pattern. Comparison of the measurements<tei:lb/>given in Table 3 emphasizes the difference in body and apertural size between these two<tei:lb/>species, furthermore, P. bryophila appears to be the only previously described species of<tei:lb/>Pontigulasia with a single internal aperture.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>ETYMOLOGY. This species is named after the geographical topography surrounding Lake<tei:lb/>Vlasina, which is mountainous (L. montana).</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Summary</tei:p>
         <tei:p>The information provided by this study extends our knowledge of the family Difflugiidae, in<tei:lb/>particular the finding of compressed species of Difflugia. The scarcity of these forms is<tei:lb/>perhaps highlighted by the review of African species in which Gauthier-Lievre &amp; Thomas<tei:lb/>(1958) list twelve compressed species, of these nine were new, out of a total of one hundred<tei:lb/>and thirty-three. Thirty-three species of Difflugia are listed here of which thirteen are re-<tei:lb/>described, including two former varieties of D. oblonga namely D. lata and D. nodosa, six<tei:lb/>new species are described D. balcanica, D. bistrica, D. dragana, D. serbica, D. serrata and<tei:lb/>D. styla the first four having compressed shells. In addition, two other new species are<tei:lb/>described Cucurbitella vlasinensis sp. nov. and Pontigulasia montana sp. nov.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>It has been mentioned before (Ogden, 19806) that the size and shape of the aperture in<tei:lb/>pyriform species of Difflugia is a relatively uniform character, but in ovoid specimens<tei:lb/>appears more variable as shown here in the description of D. lismorensis.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Morfoloska studija nekih Difflugiidae iz Jugoslavije (Rhizopoda,</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Protozoa)</tei:p>
         <tei:p>REZIME</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Podatke date u ovom radu prosiruju nasa znanja o familiji Difflugiidae, narocito u pogledu<tei:lb/>otkrivanja pljosnatih vrsta Difflugia. Retkost ovih vrsta mozda se najbolje ogleda u radu o<tei:lb/>africkim vrstama, Gauthier-Lievre i Thomas (1958), u kome je dat spisak od ukupno 133<tei:lb/>vrsta; medju njima je dvanaest pljosnatih vrsta, od kojih je devet novih. Ovaj rad sadrzi<tei:lb/>spisak od tridesettri vrste Difflugia, od kojih su trinaest ponovo opisane, ukljucujuci i dya<tei:lb/>ranija varijeteta: D. oblonga, odnosno D. lata i D. nodosa, a opisano je i sest novih<tei:lb/>vrsta D. balcanica, D. bistrica, D. dragana, D. serbica, D. serrata i D. styla, od kojih prve</tei:p>
         <tei:pb/>
      </tei:div>
      <tei:div>
         <tei:p>374 C. G. OGDEN &amp; A. 2IVKOVIC</tei:p>
         <tei:p>cetiri poseduju pljosnate ljusture. Opisane su i dve nove vrste Cucurbitella vlasinensis sp.<tei:lb/>nov. i Pontigulasia montana sp. nov.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>U ranijim publikacijama ukazano je (Ogden, 19806) da su velicina i oblik pseudostoma u<tei:lb/>piriformnim vrstama Difflugia relativno konstantna, medjutim, pojavljuje se veca vari-<tei:lb/>jabilnost u ovoidnim uzorcima, kao sto je slucaj u D. lismorensis.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Prouceni materijal sakupljen je 9 septembra 1947. godine iz jedne bare sa prostrane<tei:lb/>sfagnumske tresave na Vlasini (1200 m) koja je izgradnjom akumulacionogjezera izcezla.</tei:p>

         <tei:p>British Museum (Natural History)</tei:p>
         <tei:p>An Atlas of Freshwater Testate Amoebae</tei:p>
         <tei:p>C. G. Ogden &amp; R. H. Hedley</tei:p>
         <tei:p>1980, Hardcovers, 222pp, 17.50 (18.00 by post). Co-published by British Museum<tei:lb/>(Natural History) and Oxford University Press.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>This book illustrates, using scanning electron micrographs, most of the common<tei:lb/>species of testate amoebae that are found in freshwater habitats. Information on<tei:lb/>the biology, ecology, geographical distribution and a classification are followed by<tei:lb/>descriptions of ninety-five species. Each of these is illustrated by several views of<tei:lb/>the shell.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>The text is designed not only to enable biologists to identify species of testate<tei:lb/>amoebae, but to serve as an introduction to students interested in the taxonomy<tei:lb/>and biology of these freshwater protozoa. It will be of special interest to<tei:lb/>protozoologists, ecplogists, limnologists, water treatment specialists and<tei:lb/>micropalaeontologists interested in recent sediments.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>British Museum (Natural History)<tei:lb/>Publication Sales,<tei:lb/>Cromwell Road,<tei:lb/>London SW7 5BD.</tei:p>
